 The book is a blue print to turning the United States of America into a Third World republic, under the assumption, of course, that the republic stays together, which may be unrealistic given the authors propensity to balkanize the American public in almost every policy proposal. So the proposals go from making college education "tuition free" (i.e., paid via taxes) to "free" health care (i.e., paid via taxes). There are two key features in all of their economic proposals. Firstly, to break the link between those who benefit from a proposal and who pays for it, which obviously creates a rational incentive to over-consumption and waste (like when a large dinner table evenly divides the bill, thus creating the incentive to order expensive menu items in order not to be on the losing end of the night). Secondly, to assume that the U.S. Treasury is a bottomless resource, even though the federal debt is already 100% of GDP as of today, if you ignore the federal IOUs in the Social Security and Medicare "trust funds". Besides the economic proposals, there are proposals to favor this or that race in detriment of the other races (i.e., government-sponsored discrimination) and proposals to outlaw hugely popular classes of firearms, as if the 2nd Amendment was an afterthought. The book makes for a nauseating read unless you believe that the United States will remain wealthy and free no matter what its leaders throw at it, as if that status was a law of nature.

 If you were hoping that this book was an opportunity for in-depth analysis of complex issues, for the candidates to show that they understand complexity and demonstrate how they manage and navigate it, you're going to be disappointed.  The book is actually a giant FAQ, with each entry receiving a 1-2 page response. Since each entry is meant to stand alone it's highly repetitive, often word for word and in close proximity. Because each entry is meant to be consumed quickly, there isn't much detail.  If, for whatever reason, you need an indexed collection of talking points close at hand then this is the book for you. Otherwise, it's not.

 This book, like every other political campaign book, seeks to convince the reader of its importance. This would be an easier task with a more effective work. Weak voicing hampers the strength of the message, and the ideas aren't backed by facts but by more ideas.  One would expect a propaganda piece such as this to bring something new to the conversation, but this one instead relies on "truisms" without providing foundations. The author seems far more willing to expect the reader to accept statements made on such shaky ground - an issue that undermines the entire structure of the book.  Speaking of structure, one would expect a published work such as this to have one. This book does not - not intentionally, at least. It appears as if the author simply copied and pasted "talking points" rather than considering the framework necessary to hold it together.  At the end, the Stronger Together fails to support itself, and the entire house of cards comes tumbling down. Maybe in the hands of a more skilled writer, or at least from a mind more adept at logic and reason, this book could have found its footing.

 The book, co-authored by Clinton's running mate, Tim Kaine, sold just 2,912 copies in its first week on sale, according to Nielsen BookScan. And the online ratings have been abysmal, with 81 percent one-star ratings and an average of only 1.7 on Amazon.com after it hit book shelves on Sept 6. Amazon, however, has tried to fix that. According to WND.com -- which has been tracking the number of reviews -- Amazon deleted hundreds of comments last week that were critical of the book, which lays out a policy blueprint of how the country would look under a Clinton-Kaine administration. On Thursday, Amazon -- whose CEO, Jeff Bezos, owns the Washington Post -- said there were 91 positive reviews compared to 166 critical ones, according to WND. Just two days earlier, there were 1,244 reviews -- 81 percent of them with one-star and 16 percent with five-star ratings, the website reported. As of Monday morning, 85 percent of the customer reviews on Amazon gave it one star, while only 11 percent gave it five stars. The book dropped from No. 840 on Amazon's best-seller rankings early last week to No. 1,538 on Thursday. One reader, identified as Robert S Lionel JR, gave the book a one-star rating and wrote, "Every time I write my review it gets deleted, it's so weird. Does anyone know where the servers are hosted that contain reviews?" Another reader commented: "I expected that Amazon tweaked reviews but have lost all belief in Amazon reviews now. Will switch to Walmart for ordering most the things I used to buy here." According to Amazon's description, the book "presents [their] agenda in full, relating stories from the American people and outlining the Clinton/Kaine campaign's plans on everything from apprenticeships to the Zika virus." Many of the poor reviews appeared to hit the candidate rather than the substance of the book. Of the comments that critiqued the book, readers used words such as "boring" and "dishonest" in describing the 250-page text interspersed with bullet-point policy ideas.

 Hillary Clinton's newest book, "Stronger Together," has been met with critical reviews and slow sales since its release earlier this month.  But Amazon.com appears to be helping the Democratic presidential nominee by removing negative reviews from its website, WND.com reported.  The book, co-authored by Clinton's running mate, Tim Kaine, sold just 2,912 copies in its first week on sale, according to Nielsen BookScan. And the online ratings have been abysmal, with 81 percent one-star ratings and an average of only 1.7 on Amazon.com after it hit book shelves on Sept 6.  Amazon, however, has tried to fix that.  According to WND.com -- which has been tracking the number of reviews -- Amazon deleted hundreds of comments last week that were critical of the book, which lays out a policy blueprint of how the country would look under a Clinton-Kaine administration.  On Thursday, Amazon -- whose CEO, Jeff Bezos, owns the Washington Post -- said there were 91 positive reviews compared to 166 critical ones, according to WND. Just two days earlier, there were 1,244 reviews -- 81 percent of them with one-star and 16 percent with five-star ratings, the website reported.  As of Monday morning, 85 percent of the customer reviews on Amazon gave it one star, while only 11 percent gave it five stars.  The book dropped from No. 840 on Amazon's best-seller rankings early last week to No. 1,538 on Thursday.  One reader, identified as Robert S Lionel JR, gave the book a one-star rating and wrote, "Every time I write my review it gets deleted, it's so weird. Does anyone know where the servers are hosted that contain reviews?"  Another reader commented: "I expected that Amazon tweaked reviews but have lost all belief in Amazon reviews now. Will switch to Walmart for ordering most the things I used to buy here."  According to Amazon's description, the book "presents [their] agenda in full, relating stories from the American people and outlining the Clinton/Kaine campaign's plans on everything from apprenticeships to the Zika virus."  Many of the poor reviews appeared to hit the candidate rather than the substance of the book. Of the comments that critiqued the book, readers used words such as "boring" and "dishonest" in describing the 250-page text interspersed with bullet-point policy ideas.
 Read from cover to cover - The book contains a fairly comprehensive list of political talking points and the Clinton team's plans to address them. But, I'm not sure why we'd need to pay for this information -- and for that, I give one "star" to this opportunistic duo.

BIAS ALERT: "Hillary Clinton's newest book, "Stronger Together," has been met with critical reviews and slow sales since its release earlier this month. But Amazon.com appears to be helping the Democratic presidential nominee by removing negative reviews from its website, WND.com reported. The book, co-authored by Clinton's running mate, Tim Kaine, sold just 2,912 copies in its first week on sale, according to Nielsen BookScan. And the online ratings have been abysmal, with 81 percent one-star ratings and an average of only 1.7 on Amazon.com after it hit book shelves on Sept 6. Amazon, however, has tried to fix that. According to WND.com -- which has been tracking the number of reviews -- Amazon deleted hundreds of comments last week that were critical of the book, which lays out a policy blueprint of how the country would look under a Clinton-Kaine administration. On Thursday, Amazon -- whose CEO, Jeff Bezos, owns the Washington Post -- said there were 91 positive reviews compared to 166 critical ones, according to WND. Just two days earlier, there were 1,244 reviews -- 81 percent of them with one-star and 16 percent with five-star ratings, the website reported. As of Monday morning, 85 percent of the customer reviews on Amazon gave it one star, while only 11 percent gave it five stars. The book dropped from No. 840 on Amazon's best-seller rankings early last week to No. 1,538 on Thursday. One reader, identified as Robert S Lionel JR, gave the book a one-star rating and wrote, "Every time I write my review it gets deleted, it's so weird. Does anyone know where the servers are hosted that contain reviews?" Another reader commented: "I expected that Amazon tweaked reviews but have lost all belief in Amazon reviews now. Will switch to Walmart for ordering most the things I used to buy here." According to Amazon's description, the book "presents [their] agenda in full, relating stories from the American people and outlining the Clinton/Kaine campaign's plans on everything from apprenticeships to the Zika virus." Many of the poor reviews appeared to hit the candidate rather than the substance of the book. Of the comments that critiqued the book, readers used words such as "boring" and "dishonest" in describing the 250-page text interspersed with bullet-point policy ideas."

 It is customary for presidential candidates to have a book ghostwritten for them and released months before the election. After all, the more exposure a candidate gets (and the more shady donations one can launder as a "book deal"), the better, right? Well, not if one has so many itchy things to hide and, by simply ignoring them, said book only drives the desire to scratch them even deeper.  Let me make something very clear at this point: I am no fan of the orange, hair-plugged, narcissistic con-artist that runs against her. Nevertheless, even if one were to use this book as the only source of information, crooked-Hillary is not any better choice either.  INFLATED NON-SPEAK & NEBULOUS PROMISES The book can serve as a case study for political non-speak: how to utter words aiming to stir emotions yet manage to say absolutely nothing in the process. For instance, take the phrase "breaking down the barriers that hold Americans back": who exactly is holding Americans back and how did they manage to get away with it for so long? Is it Islam? The... French? Is the Canadians again, with their polite apologies!? No. It is the stagnated economy (the direct result of Hillary's husband deregulating the Banking sector, giving them a card-blanche to run amok with his 1999 Financial Services Modernization Act) and special interests lobbyists who siphon away jobs to slave-labor countries and then get tax exemptions for "creating jobs" in the trickle-down delusion. Does Hillary address any of these issues in the book? Don't be silly, of course not. She has slogans to repeat.  WHO IS EXACTLY THE "Together" REFERRING TO? She cannot possibly mean Americans: Hillary called more than half of them "idiots" and "irredeemable". She cannot possibly mean women: Hillary has harassed, shamed and gagged all of her husband's rape victims. And if you think that number is small, you are not paying close enough attention. And she cannot possibly mean the world: Hillary views people as inanimate stepping stones for her ambitions and the profits of her handlers. They can be assassinated, bombed, suicided (sic) or droned (now live) while she breaks in her trademark sociopath laughter. So, it must be the Bankers she has been serving all of her life, and now wants to be their willing pre-bought mouthpiece. (Puppet sold as shown. Some assembly required. Batteries in hidden device not included. Warranty does not cover brain damaging "pneumonia").  WHO IS SHE PROMISING TO MAKE "Stronger" EXACTLY? American people have been scared of the word "socialist". Quite understandably, since socialism means higher taxes (in order to support the required social infrastructure and support programs) - and who could possibly trust Washington pork-barrons with even more taxes? Trillions go missing as it is. However, American has been locked into a perpetual war for 60 years now, (WWII, Korea, South-East Asia, Vietnam, Cold War, Middle East) and taxpayers' money get blown away for nothing: the average American has seen no real benefits from all these expansive wars but empty words, flags waved (and folded) and faded bumper stickers Does Hillary promise in the book she put her name on to dismantle the perpetual war machine and instead relocate the country's resources in settling the ongoing class-war the poor are obviously losing? Is she promising to make the average American stronger? No. She is simply foreshadowing her intentions to commit even further, in an all-out war with anyone that would dare doubt she dangles two huge ones. In other words: gather provisions and get your shelters ready, she is itching to nuke Vladimir only to prove she is tough. Now, who exactly is this going to make stronger? The Military-Industrial Complex of course, silly!  DID Amazon SIDE WITH THE CORPORATE MEDIA AGENDA? I am sure there are plenty of good women and men that could run much more successful against an overinflated orange balloon.  This is, for the most part, what I want to see from the candidates. They state the issue, list the proposed solutions, then go through each solution one at a time in greater detail.  That said, first, I would have liked to see more detail. Yes, they cite substantial references, but I would like to see more specifics. Dropping this program will save money. How much? Over what time period? Adding this program will aid new graduates in starting a small business. How much will it cost? Will that cost continue after three years, or will the "catch up effect" negate it? I'm dinging it one star for being less complete than I would have liked.  I'm also dinging it a star for being repetitive. Certain stock phrases are repeated over and over. For this, the book could have used a better editor.  Overall, a fairly reasonable overview of the policies and reasoning of these candidates.
